<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Modern_narezushi">Modern <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">narezushi</i></span></h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sushi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Modern narezushi"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Funazushi_%E9%AE%92%E5%AF%BF%E5%8F%B8_Maibara_City_Shiga_Japan_2022-10-06.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Funazushi_%E9%AE%92%E5%AF%BF%E5%8F%B8_Maibara_City_Shiga_Japan_2022-10-06.jpg/250px-Funazushi_%E9%AE%92%E5%AF%BF%E5%8F%B8_Maibara_City_Shiga_Japan_2022-10-06.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="197" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Funazushi_%E9%AE%92%E5%AF%BF%E5%8F%B8_Maibara_City_Shiga_Japan_2022-10-06.jpg/500px-Funazushi_%E9%AE%92%E5%AF%BF%E5%8F%B8_Maibara_City_Shiga_Japan_2022-10-06.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1954" data-file-height="1536" /></a><figcaption><span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">Funa-zushi</i></span> (<span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">narezushi</i></span> made from <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Nigorobuna" title="Nigorobuna">nigorobuna</a></i></span>)</figcaption></figure>
<p><span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">Narezushi</i></span><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">熟れ寿司</span></span>, "matured sushi")</span> is a traditional form of fermented sushi. Skinned and gutted fish are stuffed with salt, placed in a wooden barrel, doused with salt again, then weighed down with a heavy <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Tsukemonoishi" class="mw-redirect" title="Tsukemonoishi">tsukemonoishi</a></i></span> (pickling stone). As days pass, water seeps out and is removed. After six months, this sushi can be eaten, remaining edible for another six months or more.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-hosking&#95;50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hosking-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The most famous variety of <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">narezushi</i></span> are the ones offered as a specialty <a href="/wiki/Shiga_Prefecture#Cuisine" title="Shiga Prefecture">dish of Shiga Prefecture</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> particularly the <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">funa-zushi</i></span> made from fish of the <a href="/wiki/Carassius" title="Carassius">crucian carp genus</a>, the authentic version of which calls for the use of <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Nigorobuna" title="Nigorobuna">nigorobuna</a></i></span>, a particular locally differentiated variety of <a href="/wiki/Wild_goldfish" class="mw-redirect" title="Wild goldfish">wild goldfish</a> <a href="/wiki/Endemic" class="mw-redirect" title="Endemic">endemic</a> to <a href="/wiki/Lake_Biwa" title="Lake Biwa">Lake Biwa</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;" class=""></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Nigirizushi"><i>Nigirizushi</i></h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sushi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Nigirizushi"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><span class="anchor" id="Nigiri-zushi"></span>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Onigiri" title="Onigiri">Onigiri</a>.</div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Sushi_Saito_IMG_1737_(23776728486).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Sushi_Saito_IMG_1737_%2823776728486%29.jpg/250px-Sushi_Saito_IMG_1737_%2823776728486%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Sushi_Saito_IMG_1737_%2823776728486%29.jpg/500px-Sushi_Saito_IMG_1737_%2823776728486%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="4104" data-file-height="2736" /></a><figcaption><span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">Nigirizushi</i></span></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Firefly_squid_gunkan_sushi.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Firefly_squid_gunkan_sushi.jpg/250px-Firefly_squid_gunkan_sushi.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Firefly_squid_gunkan_sushi.jpg/500px-Firefly_squid_gunkan_sushi.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1157" data-file-height="771" /></a><figcaption><span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">Gunkanmaki</i></span></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Nigirizushi_at_Luckiefun%27s_Redi_in_April_2025_close_up.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Nigirizushi_at_Luckiefun%27s_Redi_in_April_2025_close_up.jpg/250px-Nigirizushi_at_Luckiefun%27s_Redi_in_April_2025_close_up.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Nigirizushi_at_Luckiefun%27s_Redi_in_April_2025_close_up.jpg/500px-Nigirizushi_at_Luckiefun%27s_Redi_in_April_2025_close_up.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a><figcaption>Eleven pieces of nigirizushi at a sushi buffet in <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a></figcaption></figure>
<p><span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">Nigirizushi</i></span><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">握り寿司</span></span>, "hand-pressed sushi")</span> consists of an oblong mound of sushi rice that a chef typically presses between the palms of the hands to form an oval-shaped ball and a topping (the <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">neta</i></span>) draped over the ball. It is usually served with a bit of wasabi; toppings are typically fish such as salmon, tuna, or other seafood. Certain toppings are typically bound to the rice with a thin strip of nori, most commonly octopus (<span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">tako</i></span>), freshwater eel (<span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">unagi</i></span>), sea eel (<span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Anago" title="Anago">anago</a></i></span>), squid (<span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">ika</i></span>), imitation crab (<a href="/wiki/Crab_stick" title="Crab stick">kanikama</a>), and sweet egg (<span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">tamago</i></span>).
</p><p><span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">Gunkanmaki</i></span><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">軍艦巻</span></span>, "warship roll")</span> (<a href="https://ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E8%BB%8D%E8%89%A6%E5%B7%BB" class="extiw" title="ja:軍艦巻">ja:軍艦巻</a>) is a special type of <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">nigirizushi</i></span>: an oval, hand-formed clump of sushi rice that has a strip of nori wrapped around its perimeter to form a vessel that is filled with some soft, loose or fine-chopped ingredient that requires the confinement of nori such as roe, <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">nattō</i></span>, <a href="/wiki/Oyster" title="Oyster">oysters</a>, <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">uni</i></span> (sea urchin roe), sweetcorn with mayonnaise, <a href="/wiki/Scallop" title="Scallop">scallops</a>, and quail eggs. <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">Gunkan-maki</i></span> was invented at the <a href="/wiki/Ginza" title="Ginza">Ginza</a> Kyubey restaurant in 1941; its invention significantly expanded the repertoire of soft toppings used in sushi.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">Temarizushi</i></span><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">手まり寿司</span></span>, "ball sushi")</span> is a style of sushi made by pressing rice and fish into a ball-shaped form by hand using a plastic wrap.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;" class=""></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Oshizushi"><i>Oshizushi</i></h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sushi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Oshizushi"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Trichiurus_lepturus_Sushi.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Trichiurus_lepturus_Sushi.JPG/250px-Trichiurus_lepturus_Sushi.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Trichiurus_lepturus_Sushi.JPG/500px-Trichiurus_lepturus_Sushi.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Trichiurus_lepturus" class="mw-redirect" title="Trichiurus lepturus">Japanese cutlassfish</a> <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">oshizushi</i></span> at a restaurant in <a href="/wiki/Minamata,_Kumamoto" title="Minamata, Kumamoto">Minamata, Kumamoto</a></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mackerel_sushi_(sabazushi).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Mackerel_sushi_%28sabazushi%29.jpg/250px-Mackerel_sushi_%28sabazushi%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="141" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Mackerel_sushi_%28sabazushi%29.jpg/500px-Mackerel_sushi_%28sabazushi%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1440" data-file-height="810" /></a><figcaption><span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">Oshi-zushi</i></span> (pressed sushi)</figcaption></figure>
<p><span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">Oshizushi</i></span><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">押し寿司</span></span>, "pressed sushi")</span>, also known as <span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">hako-zushi</i></span><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">箱寿司</span></span>, "box sushi")</span>, is a pressed sushi from the Kansai region, a favorite and specialty of <a href="/wiki/Osaka" title="Osaka">Osaka</a>. A block-shaped piece is formed using a wooden mold, called an <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Oshizushihako" title="Oshizushihako">oshibako</a></i></span>. The chef lines the bottom of the <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">oshibako</i></span> with the toppings, covers them with sushi rice, and then presses the mold's lid to create a compact, rectilinear block. The block is removed from the mold and then cut into bite-sized pieces. Particularly famous is <span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">battera</i></span><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">バッテラ</span></span>, pressed mackerel sushi)</span> or <span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">saba zushi</i></span><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">鯖寿司</span></span>)</span>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">oshizushi</i></span>, all the ingredients are either cooked or <a href="/wiki/Cured_fish" title="Cured fish">cured</a>, and raw fish is never used.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The name <i>battera</i> means "small boat" in Portuguese (bateira), as the sushi molds resembled small boats.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p><i>Oshizushi</i> wrapped in <a href="/wiki/Persimmon" title="Persimmon">persimmon</a> leaves, a specialty of <a href="/wiki/Nara_(city)" title="Nara (city)">Nara</a>, is known as <i>kakinohazushi</i><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">柿の葉寿司</span></span>)</span>.
</p><p>Seared <i>oshizushi</i>, or <i>aburi oshizushi</i><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">炙り押し寿司</span></span>)</span>, is a popular variety invented in <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a> in 2008.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-straightaburi&#95;58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-straightaburi-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-nuvo&#95;59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nuvo-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-vancouver-oshi&#95;60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vancouver-oshi-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This involves using a <a href="/wiki/Butane_torch" title="Butane torch">butane torch</a> to sear the sushi, which may contain ingredients such as mayonnaise, various sauces, <a href="/wiki/Jalape%C3%B1o" title="Jalapeño">jalapeños</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Avocado" title="Avocado">avocado</a> in addition to typical sushi ingredients such as salmon and <a href="/wiki/Mackerel_as_food" title="Mackerel as food">mackerel</a>. The variety has since spread to other cities, such as <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-torontoaburi&#95;61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-torontoaburi-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;" class=""></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Western-style_sushi">Western-style sushi</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sushi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Western-style sushi"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Norwegia_Roll_Salmon_Sushi.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Norwegia_Roll_Salmon_Sushi.jpg/250px-Norwegia_Roll_Salmon_Sushi.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="181" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Norwegia_Roll_Salmon_Sushi.jpg/500px-Norwegia_Roll_Salmon_Sushi.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="2551" data-file-height="1848" /></a><figcaption>Norway roll<span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">ノルウェー巻き</span></span>)</span>. A Norwegian businessman introduced the use of salmon as a sushi ingredient to Japan in the 1980s.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-desperate&#95;62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-desperate-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>The increasing popularity of sushi worldwide has resulted in variations typically found in the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western world</a> but rarely in Japan.
</p><p>One widespread form of sushi created to suit the Western palate is the <a href="/wiki/California_roll" title="California roll">California roll</a>, a <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="#Makizushi">norimaki</a></i></span> which presently almost always uses <a href="/wiki/Crab_stick" title="Crab stick">imitation crab</a> (the original recipe calls for real cooked crab), along with avocado and cucumber.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A wide variety of popular rolls (<span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">norimaki</i></span> and <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="#Uramaki">uramaki</a></i></span>) have evolved since. 
</p><p>The identity of the creator of the California roll is disputed. Several chefs from <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> have been cited as the dish's originators, as well as one chef from <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The earliest mention in print of a "California roll" was in the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> and an <a href="/wiki/Ocala,_Florida" title="Ocala, Florida">Ocala, Florida</a> newspaper on November 25, 1979.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:1&#95;65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Less than a month later an <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> story credited a Los Angeles chef named Ken Seusa at the Kin Jo sushi restaurant near <a href="/wiki/Hollywood,_Los_Angeles" title="Hollywood, Los Angeles">Hollywood</a> as its inventor. The AP article cited Mrs. Fuji Wade, manager of the restaurant, as its source for the claim.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:1&#95;65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p>Others<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:2&#95;66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:3&#95;67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:4&#95;68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> attribute the dish to Ichiro Mashita, another Los Angeles sushi <a href="/wiki/Chef" title="Chef">chef</a> from the former <a href="/wiki/Little_Tokyo,_Los_Angeles" title="Little Tokyo, Los Angeles">Little Tokyo</a> restaurant "Tokyo Kaikan".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to this account, Mashita began substituting the <i><a href="/wiki/Ch%C5%ABtoro" class="mw-redirect" title="Chūtoro">toro</a></i> (fatty tuna) with avocado in the off-season, and after further experimentation, developed the prototype, back in the 1960s.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Japanese-born chef <a href="/wiki/Hidekazu_Tojo" title="Hidekazu Tojo">Hidekazu Tojo</a>, a resident of Vancouver, British Columbia since 1971 is also credited,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:2&#95;66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:3&#95;67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:4&#95;68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> claiming he created the California roll at his restaurant in the late 1970s.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Tojo insists he is the innovator of the "inside-out" sushi, and it got the name "California roll" because its contents of crab and avocado were abbreviated to C.A., which is the abbreviation for the state of <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>. Because of this coincidence, Tojo was set on the name California Roll. According to Tojo, he single-handedly created the California roll at his Vancouver, British Columbia restaurant, including all the modern ingredients of cucumber, cooked crab, and avocado.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2016 the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Agriculture,_Forestry_and_Fisheries_(Japan)" title="Ministry of Agriculture, Forestry and Fisheries (Japan)">Japanese Ministry of Agriculture, Forestry and Fisheries</a> named Tojo a <a href="/wiki/Goodwill_ambassador" title="Goodwill ambassador">goodwill ambassador</a> for Japanese cuisine.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The common theme in origin stories is that surrounding the roll in rice made it more appealing to western consumers who had never eaten traditional sushi. This innovation led to the eventual creation of countless rolls across North America and the world.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2024)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>For example, the "Norway roll" is another variant of <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">uramakizushi</i></span> filled with <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">tamago</i></span> (omelette), imitation crab and cucumber, rolled with <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">shiso</i></span> leaf and <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">nori</i></span>, topped with slices of Norwegian salmon, garnished with lemon and mayonnaise.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Although most Western sushi creations are rare in Japan, a notable exception to this is the use of salmon. The Japanese have eaten salmon since prehistory; however, caught salmon in nature often contains <a href="/wiki/Parasitism" title="Parasitism">parasites</a> and must be cooked or cured for its lean meat to be edible. On the other side of the world, in the 1960s and 1970s, Norwegian entrepreneurs started experimenting with <a href="/wiki/Aquaculture" title="Aquaculture">aquaculture</a> farming. The big breakthrough was when they figured out how to raise salmon in net pens in the sea. Being farm-raised, the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_salmon" title="Atlantic salmon">Atlantic salmon</a> reportedly showed advantages over the <a href="/wiki/Oncorhynchus" title="Oncorhynchus">Pacific salmon</a>, such as no parasites, easy animal capture, and higher fat content. With government subsidies and improved techniques, they were so successful in raising fatty and parasite-free salmon they ended up with a surplus. Norway has a small population and limited market; therefore, they looked to other countries to export their salmon. The first Norwegian salmon was imported into Japan in 1980, accepted conventionally, for grilling, not for sushi. Salmon had already been consumed in North America as an ingredient in sushi as early as the 1970s.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Salmon sushi did not become widely accepted in Japan until a successful marketing partnership in the late 1980s between <a href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B8rn_E._Olsen" title="Bjørn E. Olsen">Bjørn E. Olsen</a>, a Norwegian businessman tasked with helping the Norwegian salmon industry glut, and the Japanese food supplier <a href="/wiki/Nichirei" title="Nichirei">Nichirei</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-NorwegianSalmonIntroduction&#95;79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwegianSalmonIntroduction-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-desperate&#95;62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-desperate-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Uramaki"><i>Uramaki</i></h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sushi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Uramaki"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Uramaki" redirects here. For the song, see <a href="/wiki/Uramaki_(song)" title="Uramaki (song)">Uramaki (song)</a>.</div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Western_Sushi.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Western_Sushi.jpg/250px-Western_Sushi.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="166" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Western_Sushi.jpg/500px-Western_Sushi.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a><figcaption><span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">Uramakizushi</i></span> rolls</figcaption></figure>
<p><span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">Uramaki</i></span><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">裏巻</span></span>, "inside-out roll")</span> is a medium-sized cylindrical style of sushi with two or more fillings and was developed as a result of the creation of the California roll, as a method originally meant to hide the nori. <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">Uramaki</i></span> differs from other <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">makimono</i></span> because the rice is on the outside and the nori inside. The filling is surrounded by nori, then a layer of rice, and optionally an outer coating of some other ingredients such as roe or toasted sesame seeds. It can be made with different fillings, such as tuna, <a href="/wiki/Crab_meat" title="Crab meat">crab meat</a>, avocado, mayonnaise, cucumber, or carrots.
</p><p>Examples of variations include the <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_roll" title="Rainbow roll">rainbow roll</a> (an inside-out topped with thinly sliced <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">maguro, hamachi, ebi, sake</i></span> and avocado) and the caterpillar roll (an inside-out topped with thinly sliced avocado). Also commonly found is the "rock and roll" (an inside-out roll with barbecued freshwater eel and avocado with toasted sesame seeds on the outside).
</p><p>In Japan, <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">uramaki</i></span> is an uncommon type of <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">makimono</i></span>; because sushi is traditionally eaten by hand in Japan, the outer layer of rice can be quite difficult to handle with fingers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-sushimasters&#95;80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sushimasters-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In Brazil <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">uramaki</i></span> and other sushi pieces commonly include cream cheese in their recipe. Although unheard of in Japanese sushi, this is the most common sushi ingredient used in Brazil. <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">Temaki</i></span> also often contains a large amount of cream cheese and is extremely popular in restaurants.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="American-style_makizushi">American-style <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">makizushi</i></span></h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sushi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: American-style makizushi"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Golden_Maki_Rainbow_Roll_sushi.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Golden_Maki_Rainbow_Roll_sushi.jpg/250px-Golden_Maki_Rainbow_Roll_sushi.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Golden_Maki_Rainbow_Roll_sushi.jpg/500px-Golden_Maki_Rainbow_Roll_sushi.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2250" /></a><figcaption>Rainbow roll, <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">uramaki</i></span> with multiple fillings including shrimp tempura, salmon, avocado, mango, with rice mixed with <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">tobiko</i></span></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Sushi_and_Sashimi.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Sushi_and_Sashimi.jpg/250px-Sushi_and_Sashimi.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="126" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Sushi_and_Sashimi.jpg/500px-Sushi_and_Sashimi.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="3702" data-file-height="1869" /></a><figcaption>Dragon roll, <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">uramaki</i></span> with multiple fillings including crab meat, cucumber, avocado, with rice topped with eel and avocado</figcaption></figure>
<p>Multiple-filling rolls inspired by <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="#Makizushi">futomaki</a></i></span> are a more popular type of sushi within the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and come in variations that take their names from their places of origin. Other rolls may include a variety of ingredients, including chopped scallops, spicy tuna, beef or chicken <a href="/wiki/Teriyaki" title="Teriyaki">teriyaki</a> roll, <a href="/wiki/Okra" title="Okra">okra</a>, and assorted vegetables such as cucumber and avocado, and the <a href="/wiki/Tempura" title="Tempura">tempura</a> roll, where shrimp tempura is inside the roll or the entire roll is battered and fried tempura-style. In the Southern United States, many sushi restaurants prepare rolls using <a href="/wiki/Crawfish" class="mw-redirect" title="Crawfish">crawfish</a>. Sometimes, rolls are made with brown rice or black rice, known as forbidden rice, which appear in Japanese cuisine as well.
</p><p>Per <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration" title="Food and Drug Administration">Food and Drug Administration</a> regulations, raw fish served in the United States must be frozen before serving to kill parasites.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Since rolls are often made to order, it is not unusual for the customer to specify the exact ingredients desired (e.g., salmon roll, cucumber roll, avocado roll, tuna roll, shrimp or tuna tempura roll, etc.). Though the menu names of dishes often vary by restaurant, some examples include the following:
</p>

</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>
</td>
<td>Boston roll
</td>
<td>An <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">uramaki</i></span> California roll with <a href="/wiki/Poaching_(cooking)" title="Poaching (cooking)">poached</a> shrimp instead of <a href="/wiki/Imitation_crab" class="mw-redirect" title="Imitation crab">imitation crab</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:BC_Roll.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/BC_Roll.jpg/120px-BC_Roll.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="90" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/BC_Roll.jpg/250px-BC_Roll.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1936" /></a></span>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/B.C._roll" title="B.C. roll">British Columbia roll</a>
</td>
<td>A roll containing grilled or barbecued salmon skin, cucumber, and sweet sauce, sometimes with roe. Also sometimes referred to as salmon skin rolls outside of <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, Canada.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Maki_a_un_restaurant_japon%C3%A9s_de_X%C3%A0bia.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Maki_a_un_restaurant_japon%C3%A9s_de_X%C3%A0bia.jpg/120px-Maki_a_un_restaurant_japon%C3%A9s_de_X%C3%A0bia.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="88" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Maki_a_un_restaurant_japon%C3%A9s_de_X%C3%A0bia.jpg/250px-Maki_a_un_restaurant_japon%C3%A9s_de_X%C3%A0bia.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="3859" data-file-height="2838" /></a></span>
</td>
<td>California roll
</td>
<td>A roll consisting of avocado, <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">kani kama</i></span> (imitation crab/<a href="/wiki/Crab_stick" title="Crab stick">crab stick</a>) (also can contain real crab in "premium" varieties), cucumber, and <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Tobiko" title="Tobiko">tobiko</a></i></span>, often made as <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">uramaki</i></span> (with rice on the outside, nori on the inside).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Golden_Maki_Vegetarian_Dragon_sushi_roll.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Golden_Maki_Vegetarian_Dragon_sushi_roll.jpg/120px-Golden_Maki_Vegetarian_Dragon_sushi_roll.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="90" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Golden_Maki_Vegetarian_Dragon_sushi_roll.jpg/250px-Golden_Maki_Vegetarian_Dragon_sushi_roll.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2250" /></a></span>
</td>
<td>Dragon roll
</td>
<td>A roll containing fillings such as shrimp tempura, cucumber, and unagi, and wrapped distinctively with avocado on the outside. Also commonly called a "caterpillar roll", its avocado exterior is said to resemble the scales of a dragon.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Dynamite_rolls.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Dynamite_rolls.jpg/120px-Dynamite_rolls.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="91" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Dynamite_rolls.jpg/250px-Dynamite_rolls.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1211" data-file-height="919" /></a></span>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Dynamite_roll" title="Dynamite roll">Dynamite roll</a>
</td>
<td>A roll including yellowtail (<span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">hamachi</i></span>) or prawn tempura, and fillings such as bean sprouts, carrots, avocado, cucumber, chili, spicy mayonnaise, and roe.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>
</td>
<td>Hawaiian roll
</td>
<td>A roll containing <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Sh%C5%8Dyu" class="mw-redirect" title="Shōyu">shōyu</a></i></span> tuna (canned), <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Tamagoyaki" title="Tamagoyaki">tamago</a></i></span>, <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">kanpyō</i></span>, <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Kamaboko" title="Kamaboko">kamaboko</a></i></span>, and the distinctive red and green <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">hana ebi</i></span> (shrimp powder).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>
</td>
<td>Mango roll
</td>
<td>A roll including fillings such as avocado, crab meat, tempura shrimp, and mango slices, and topped off with a creamy mango paste.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>
</td>
<td>Michigan roll
</td>
<td>A roll including fillings such as spicy tuna, smelt roe, spicy sauce, avocado, and sushi rice. It is a variation on a spicy tuna roll.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>
</td>
<td>New Mexico roll
</td>
<td>A roll originating in <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>; includes <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico_green_chile" class="mw-redirect" title="New Mexico green chile">New Mexico green chile</a> (sometimes tempura-fried), teriyaki sauce, and rice.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Sometimes simply referred to as a "green chile (tempura) roll" within the state.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Philly_roll.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Philly_roll.jpg/120px-Philly_roll.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="120" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Philly_roll.jpg/250px-Philly_roll.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="2262" data-file-height="2262" /></a></span>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_roll" title="Philadelphia roll">Philadelphia roll</a>
</td>
<td>A roll consisting of raw or smoked salmon and <a href="/wiki/Cream_cheese" title="Cream cheese">cream cheese</a> (the name refers to <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_cream_cheese" class="mw-redirect" title="Philadelphia cream cheese">Philadelphia cream cheese</a>), with cucumber, avocado, and/or scallion.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Functionally synonymous with Japanese bagel (JB) roll and Seattle roll.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Golden_Maki_Rainbow_Roll_sushi.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Golden_Maki_Rainbow_Roll_sushi.jpg/120px-Golden_Maki_Rainbow_Roll_sushi.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="90" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Golden_Maki_Rainbow_Roll_sushi.jpg/250px-Golden_Maki_Rainbow_Roll_sushi.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2250" /></a></span>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Rainbow_roll" title="Rainbow roll">Rainbow roll</a>
</td>
<td>A California <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">uramaki</i></span> roll with multiple types of fish (commonly yellowtail, tuna, salmon, snapper, white fish, eel, etc.) and avocado wrapped around it.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</td></tr>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Australia">Australia</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sushi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Australia"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
